       &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-antrun-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;        &lt;version&gt;1.7&lt;/version&gt;&#010;        ...&#010;            &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;              &lt;target&gt;&#010;                &lt;ant antfile="build.xml" target="build" /&gt;&#010;              &lt;/target&gt;&#010;            &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;        ...&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;build.xml looks like:&#010;&lt;?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?&gt;&#010;&lt;project&gt;&#010;  &lt;target name="build"&gt;&#010;    &lt;antversion property="antversion"/&gt;&#010;    &lt;echo&gt;Using Ant v${antversion}&lt;/echo&gt;&#010;    &lt;sshexec host="ansades51" username="emob" password="emob" trust="true" command="echo&#010;hello" outputproperty="ssh.cmd" /&gt;&#010;    &lt;echo&gt;${ssh.cmd}&lt;/echo&gt;&#010;  &lt;/target&gt;&#010;&lt;/project&gt;&#010;&#010;When calling build.xml via Maven, the output I get is:&#010;[INFO] --- maven-antrun-plugin:1.7:run (default) @ ant.test ---&#010;[INFO] Executing tasks&#010;main:&#010;build:&#010; Name  :- 
Dan Tran &lt;dant...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Pack with native tar, unpack with maven-dependency-plugin failure  
Date  :-
Mon, 02 Jun 2014 23:27:13 GMT  
contents:- 
I found the root cause of this issue where  I need to force a '-z' option&#010;during native tar compression.  Without this flag, the output is just a&#010;normal tar file where native tar is very smart to figure this out. Where&#010;are plexus-archiver only looks for gz signature and bails out.&#010;&#010;Thanks&#010;&#010;-Dan&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Jun 2, 2014 at 11:47 AM, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hi&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have a number of tar.gz artifacts packed with cygwin/linux tar, but&#010;&gt; maven-dependency-plugin fails to unpack with with the following error (&#010;&gt; have you seen this)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Caused by: java.util.zip.ZipException: Not in GZIP format&#010;&gt; at java.util.zip.GZIPInputStream.readHeader(GZIPInputStream.java:164)&#010;&gt; at java.util.zip.GZIPInputStream.&lt;init&gt;(GZIPInputStream.java:78)&#010;&gt;  at java.util.zip.GZIPInputStream.&lt;init&gt;(GZIPInputStream.java:90)&#010;&gt; at&#010;&gt; org.codehaus.plexus.archiver.tar.TarUnArchiver$UntarCompressionMethod.decompress(TarUnArchiver.java:191)&#010;&gt;  at&#010;&gt; org.codehaus.plexus.archiver.tar.TarUnArchiver$UntarCompressionMethod.access$000(TarUnArchiver.java:112)&#010;&gt; at&#010;&gt; org.codehaus.plexus.archiver.tar.TarUnArchiver.execute(TarUnArchiver.java:86)&#010;&gt;  ... 26 more&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -Dan&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Hi Dan,&#010;&#010;Dan Tran wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I found the root cause of this issue where  I need to force a '-z' option&#010;&gt; during native tar compression.  Without this flag, the output is just a&#010;&gt; normal tar file where native tar is very smart to figure this out. Where&#010;&gt; are plexus-archiver only looks for gz signature and bails out.&#010;&#010;You may always use the "file" utility to get an idea of the real file &#010;format:&#010;&#010;================= %&lt; =================&#010;~/tmp $ tar cf test-tar.tar.gz *.txt&#010;~/tmp $ tar czf test-gz.tar.gz *.txt&#010;~/tmp $ tar cjf test-bz2.tar.gz *.txt&#010;~/tmp $ file *.tar.gz&#010;test-bz2.tar.gz: bzip2 compressed data, block size = 900k&#010;test-gz.tar.gz:  gzip compressed data, last modified: Tue Jun  3 07:50:26 &#010;2014, from Unix&#010;test-tar.tar.gz: POSIX tar archive (GNU)&#010;================= %&lt; =================&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

question about sharing assembly descriptor  
Date  :-
Mon, 02 Jun 2014 21:16:53 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello *,&#010;&#009;I have a problem when using the sharing assembly descriptors. Let’s say i have a directory&#010;structure loos like:&#010;&#010;module-A&#010;    +-- src&#010;    |   `-- main&#010;    |       `-- resources&#010;    |           `-- assemblies&#010;    |               `-- myassembly.xml&#010;    `— pom.xml&#010;module-B&#010;    `—pom.xml&#010;&#010;&#010;module-B’s pom.xml wants to use the descriptor in module-A, which could be done by adding&#010;module-A as a dependency on the assembly plugin then use the descriptorRefs. But the problem&#010;is I already has module B as a dependency in module-A. so this will lead to a cyclic reference.&#010;&#010;If i do without the dependency and just use the descriptor directly will also lead to wrong&#010;base directory for the descriptor.(the base directory for myassembly.xml will be module-B)&#010;&#010;&#010;How can i use the shared assembly descriptor in this case properly?&#010;&#010;Best,&#010;Mingliang&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

Create a third modul with just the assembly descriptor:&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin/examples/sharing-descriptors.html&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Jun 2, 2014 at 11:16 PM, Mingliang Qi &lt;qmlmoon@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello *,&#010;&gt;         I have a problem when using the sharing assembly descriptors.&#010;&gt; Let’s say i have a directory structure loos like:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; module-A&#010;&gt;     +-- src&#010;&gt;     |   `-- main&#010;&gt;     |       `-- resources&#010;&gt;     |           `-- assemblies&#010;&gt;     |               `-- myassembly.xml&#010;&gt;     `— pom.xml&#010;&gt; module-B&#010;&gt;     `—pom.xml&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; module-B’s pom.xml wants to use the descriptor in module-A, which could be&#010;&gt; done by adding module-A as a dependency on the assembly plugin then use the&#010;&gt; descriptorRefs. But the problem is I already has module B as a dependency&#010;&gt; in module-A. so this will lead to a cyclic reference.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If i do without the dependency and just use the descriptor directly will&#010;&gt; also lead to wrong base directory for the descriptor.(the base directory&#010;&gt; for myassembly.xml will be module-B)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; How can i use the shared assembly descriptor in this case properly?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Best,&#010;&gt; Mingliang&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Nexus / Maven repository artifact handling   
Date  :-
Mon, 02 Jun 2014 22:06:22 GMT  
contents:- 
&#010;We have a Nexus server to which various projects upload artifacts. &#010;The artifacts are uploaded to a release repository, not a snapshot repository. &#010;&#010;One project is just a consumer of the artifacts.  It does not upload anything. &#010;&#010;Even though we have an updated artifact available, the consuming project does not download&#010;the artifacts from nexus until we clear out the local repo in ~/.m2.  &#010;&#010;How does Nexus / Maven determine that a new artifact needs to be downloaded from the remote&#010;repo?  The timestamp reflects the time of upload of the artifact.  So what am I missing ?&#010;&#010;&#010;The GAV is of the form:&#010;&#010;     group:artifact.id:group.artifact.id-11.1.0.jar&#010;&#010;When a new group.artifact.id-11.1.0.jar is uploaded, it won't get downloaded by the consuming&#010;project. &#010;&#010;&#010;cheers,   &#010;&#010;         mehul &#010;&#010;--&#010;Sent from my "smart" phone&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Jason van Zyl &lt;ja...@takari.io&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Nexus / Maven repository artifact handling  
Date  :-
Mon, 02 Jun 2014 22:54:13 GMT  
contents:- 
Are you deploying different artifacts with the same version? Release versions are expected&#010;to be immutable and Maven will not try to download a released artifact again because it's&#010;not expected to change. If you are deploying different artifacts using the same version you&#010;are using Maven incorrectly.&#010;&#010;On Jun 2, 2014, at 6:06 PM, mehul.sanghvi@gmail.com wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; We have a Nexus server to which various projects upload artifacts. &#010;&gt; The artifacts are uploaded to a release repository, not a snapshot repository. &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; One project is just a consumer of the artifacts.  It does not upload anything. &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Even though we have an updated artifact available, the consuming project does not download&#010;the artifacts from nexus until we clear out the local repo in ~/.m2.  &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; How does Nexus / Maven determine that a new artifact needs to be downloaded from the&#010;remote repo?  The timestamp reflects the time of upload of the artifact.  So what am I missing&#010;? &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; The GAV is of the form:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;     group:artifact.id:group.artifact.id-11.1.0.jar&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; When a new group.artifact.id-11.1.0.jar is uploaded, it won't get downloaded by the consuming&#010;project. &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; cheers,   &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;         mehul &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; Sent from my "smart" phone&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Jason&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------&#010;Jason van Zyl&#010;Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

Re: Nexus / Maven repository artifact handling  
Date  :-
Tue, 03 Jun 2014 02:27:33 GMT  
contents:- 
We use SNAPSHOT during development, say 1.1.0-SNAPSHOT.  At code freeze, we&#010;branch off from main line to a version specific branch and remove SNAPSHOT&#010;from the version string, so it becomes 1.1.0.  Between code freeze and&#010;release we have RC builds.  Its at that point that when a newer build of&#010;the same artifact is uploaded, so the GAV is identical,&#010;maven will not download the newest build.  So its the same JAR file being&#010;uploaded, with the same version.  The only thing changing is the file size&#010;and time stamp of the uploaded&#010;artifact.&#010;&#010;So I have fubar-1.1.0.jar uploaded to Nexus.  The consumer picks up this&#010;jar file and downloads to ~/.m2.  Now we find some problems with it, and&#010;there is an update.  So a newer&#010;fubar-1.1.0.jar is uploaded, over-writing the old one.  Then next time a&#010;build of the consuming project is run, it does not download the newly built&#010;fubar-1.1.0.jar.  Based on what&#010;you're saying, this is a feature and the right way to do things, correct ?&#010;&#010;&#010;Than, how do folks handle RC versions ?&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;cheers,&#010;&#010;     mehul&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Jun 2, 2014 at 6:54 PM, Jason van Zyl &lt;jason@takari.io&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Are you deploying different artifacts with the same version? It does not upload&#010;&gt; anything.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Even though we have an updated artifact available, the consuming project&#010;&gt; does not download the artifacts from nexus until we clear out the local&#010;&gt; repo in ~/.m2.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; How does Nexus / Maven determine that a new artifact needs to be&#010;&gt; downloaded from the remote repo?  The timestamp reflects the time of upload&#010;&gt; of the artifact.  So what am I missing ?&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The GAV is of the form:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;     group:artifact.id:group.artifact.id-11.1.0.jar&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; When a new group.artifact.id-11.1.0.jar is uploaded, it won't get&#010;&gt; downloaded by the consuming project.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; cheers,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;         mehul&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; --&#010;&gt; &gt; Sent from my "smart" phone&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Jason&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ----------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; Jason van Zyl&#010;&gt; Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;&gt; http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;&gt; http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Mehul N. Mehul, this is the wrong pattern to use. It goes against the entire Maven&#010;dependency mechanism.&#010;&#010;Each GAV (aside from snapsghots) should represent a unique build.&#010;&#010;You should be creating new RC GAVs for each release candidate. eg&#010;groupX-artifactX-versionZ.rc1&#010;&#010;William&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Jun 3, 2014 at 12:27 PM, Mehul Sanghvi &lt;mehul.sanghvi@gmail.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; We use SNAPSHOT during development, say 1.1.0-SNAPSHOT.  At code freeze, we&#010;&gt; branch off from main line to a version specific branch and remove SNAPSHOT&#010;&gt; from the version string, so it becomes 1.1.0.  Between code freeze and&#010;&gt; release we have RC builds.  Its at that point that when a newer build of&#010;&gt; the same artifact is uploaded, so the GAV is identical,&#010;&gt; maven will not download the newest build.  So its the same JAR file being&#010;&gt; uploaded, with the same version.  The only thing changing is the file size&#010;&gt; and time stamp of the uploaded&#010;&gt; artifact.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So I have fubar-1.1.0.jar uploaded to Nexus.  The consumer picks up this&#010;&gt; jar file and downloads to ~/.m2.  Now we find some problems with it, and&#010;&gt; there is an update.  So a newer&#010;&gt; fubar-1.1.0.jar is uploaded, over-writing the old one.  Then next time a&#010;&gt; build of the consuming project is run, it does not download the newly built&#010;&gt; fubar-1.1.0.jar.  Based on what&#010;&gt; you're saying, this is a feature and the right way to do things, correct ?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Than, how do folks handle RC versions ?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; cheers,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;      mehul&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Mon, Jun 2, 2014 at 6:54 PM, Jason van Zyl &lt;jason@takari.io&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Are you deploying different artifacts with the same version? Date  :-

contents:- 
Windows does not have tar by default. You need to install Git (incl. Git Bash), Cygwin, GnuWin32&#010;or similar. I would not expect any user to have tar installed at all or if so then in any&#010;predictable location or even reachable via PATH.&#010;-- &#010;Alexander Kriegisch&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; Am 03.06.2014 um 00:36 schrieb Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I am think of enhancing maven-dependency-plugin by adding option  to unpack&#010;&gt; 'tar' like artifact using native tar since it is faster and reserve soft&#010;&gt; links (?)&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thoughts? would it be a maintaining night mare??&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -Dan&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

There isn't any particular reason for moving off of Nexus.  We have Nexus&#010;as its the most common repository manager used.  I want to do an evaluation&#010;before we make the decision to go with one or the other and whether to get&#010;the paid version or stick to the free version.  Archiva, Artifactory, and&#010;Nexus are my choices.  Part of the evaluation will be to take a look at our&#010;processes, see where and how we can leverage a repository manager.&#010;&#010;Currently we use something that was written internally earlier this&#010;century, in JHTML and JSP, which hasn't been updated since and is difficult&#010;to update and maintain.  I want to modernise by shifting things away from&#010;the home grown solution.  We've got groups using Ant, Maven, and homegrown&#010;Perl based build tools, and Make, and I have no idea what else is lurking&#010;out there.  Some of those will need ways to upload to the repository&#010;manager.&#010;&#010;That's the back story to it.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Jun 3, 2014 at 3:22 PM, Glenn Brown &lt;ghbrown60640@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I would not recommend Archiva. It's intended to be mainly a reference&#010;&gt; implementation of the repository and, personally, i find it's UI to be a&#010;&gt; bit clunky. I was more looking for gotchas that people may have run&#010;&gt; &gt; into when doing a migration and/or what they took into account when&#010;&gt; &gt; choosing a system. Subject  :-
Controlling order of plugin execution  
Date  :-
Tue, 03 Jun 2014 19:48:07 GMT  
contents:- 
I'm trying to set up a Maven build for CI/CD, and one of the requirements for testing is to&#010;create, populate and tweak a database schema.&#010;&#010;This involves interleaving various executions of maven-dependency-plugin, sql-maven-plugin&#010;and exec-maven-plugin, and there aren't enough lifecycle phases *-test-[re]sources to accommodate&#010;all the steps. &#010;&#010;I'd like to bind six executions as follows:&#010;&#010;    1 maven-dependency-plugin:unpack -&gt; generate-test-resources&#010;    2 sql-maven-plugin:execute       -&gt; generate-test-resources&#010;    3 sql-maven-plugin:execute       -&gt; generate-test-resources&#010;    4 exec-maven-plugin:exec         -&gt; process-test-resources&#010;    5 exec-maven-plugin:exec         -&gt; process-test-resources&#010;    6 sql-maven-plugin:execute       -&gt; process-test-resources&#010;&#010;But this doesn't work as Maven wants to execute sql-maven-plugin (steps 2 &amp; 3) before&#010;step 1 and I can't find a way to make it do things in the desired sequence.&#010;&#010;There's a bug in Jira for this http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MNG-3522 but it was closed&#010;as part of the "great Jira cleanup of 2014".&#010;&#010;This has been an issue for several years but seems to get no attention.  I don't think I should&#010;be required to write my own plugin to do what should be a common requirement.&#010;&#010;Can someone explain if there's an approved way to accomplish this? &#010;&#010;I know Maven is supposed to be declarative in nature, but sequencing steps seems like a basic&#010;requirement.  From the lack of attention, and from reading other posts in places like StackOverflow,&#010;it appears there may be a philosophical objection to explicitly ordering executions.  Can&#010;someone explain the reasoning for this?&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

jhgnwea &lt;jim.garri...@nwea.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Controlling order of plugin execution  
Date  :-
Wed, 04 Jun 2014 15:47:15 GMT  
contents:- 
Paul Benedict wrote&#010;&gt; I agree with Dan. Last I check, IIRC, the order of operations of plugins&#010;&gt; is&#010;&gt; defined by their sequential order in the POM. However, I also find this a&#010;&gt; bit problematic with inheritance -- I don't know off the top of my head&#010;&gt; what happens then.&#010;&#010;Ordering applies only for executions of a single plugin.  If you need to&#010;interleave executions of two or more plugins you're out of luck.  Say you&#010;have two plugins, exec-maven and maven-sql, and want to run &#010;&#010;    exec-maven A1&#010;    maven-sql B1&#010;    exec-maven A2&#010;    maven-sql B2&#010;&#010;A1 and A2 will run in that order, and (B1, B2) will be ordered, but you&#010;can't control which set (A or B) runs first without horribly abusing the&#010;phase bindings.  And, if you have a more complex sequence with 3  plugins&#010;and multiple executions of each, there aren't enough available phases to&#010;successfully order everything.&#010;&#010;It should be possible to bind multiple plugin executions, of DIFFERENT&#010;plugins, to a single phase and deterministically specify the execution&#010;order.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Controlling-order-of-plugin-execution-tp5794777p5794892.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Re: Controlling order of plugin execution

contents:- 
That's usually a sign that you have wandered off The Maven Way™&#010;&#010;There are ways back onto the blessed path... they typically involve writing&#010;a plugin&#010;&#010;&#010;On 4 June 2014 16:47, jhgnwea &lt;jim.garrison@nwea.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Paul Benedict wrote&#010;&gt; &gt; I agree with Dan. Last I check, IIRC, the order of operations of plugins&#010;&gt; &gt; is&#010;&gt; &gt; defined by their sequential order in the POM. However, I also find this a&#010;&gt; &gt; bit problematic with inheritance -- I don't know off the top of my head&#010;&gt; &gt; what happens then.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ordering applies only for executions of a single plugin.  If you need to&#010;&gt; interleave executions of two or more plugins you're out of luck.  Say you&#010;&gt; have two plugins, exec-maven and maven-sql, and want to run&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     exec-maven A1&#010;&gt;     maven-sql B1&#010;&gt;     exec-maven A2&#010;&gt;     maven-sql B2&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A1 and A2 will run in that order, and (B1, B2) will be ordered, but you&#010;&gt; can't control which set (A or B) runs first without horribly abusing the&#010;&gt; phase bindings.  And, if you have a more complex sequence with 3  plugins&#010;&gt; and multiple executions of each, there aren't enough available phases to&#010;&gt; successfully order everything.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; It should be possible to bind multiple plugin executions, of DIFFERENT&#010;&gt; plugins, to a single phase and deterministically specify the execution&#010;&gt; order.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Controlling-order-of-plugin-execution-tp5794777p5794892.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

And, if you have a more complex sequence with 3&#010;&gt; &gt; plugins&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; and multiple executions of each, there aren't enough available&#010;&gt; &gt; phases to&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; successfully order everything.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; It should be possible to bind multiple plugin executions, of&#010;&gt; &gt; DIFFERENT&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; plugins, to a single phase and deterministically specify the&#010;&gt; &gt; execution&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; order.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Sorry, I disagree. I'm really curious why there's a strong philosophical&#010;&gt; objection to requesting this enhancement.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Is it unreasonable to suggest that "The Maven Way" is not perfect and&#010;&gt; might need some adjustments to handle common use-cases the original&#010;&gt; designers didn't foresee?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Is my goal of using Maven to automate CI/CD, which can involve configuring&#010;&gt; external resources by running various plugins in a specific sequence,&#010;&gt; somehow in violation of "the Maven way"?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Consider the phrase "...you have wandered off The Maven Way™".  I can't&#010;&gt; tell if you intended this ironically or seriously.  If it's the latter, it&#010;&gt; seems like you're saying is "Maven is perfect. If Maven doesn't handle your&#010;&gt; use-case, then your use-case is invalid".  Is that true?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Last I check, IIRC, the order of operations of&#010;&gt; &gt; plugins&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; is&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; defined by their sequential order in the POM. However, I also find&#010;&gt; &gt; this a&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; bit problematic with inheritance -- I don't know off the top of my&#010;&gt; &gt; head&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; what happens then.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Ordering applies only for executions of a single plugin.  If you&#010;&gt; &gt; need to&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; interleave executions of two or more plugins you're out of luck.&#010;&gt; &gt; Say you&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; have two plugins, exec-maven and maven-sql, and want to run&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;     exec-maven A1&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;     maven-sql B1&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;     exec-maven A2&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;     maven-sql B2&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; A1 and A2 will run in that order, and (B1, B2) will be ordered, but&#010;&gt; &gt; you&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; can't control which set (A or B) runs first without horribly abusing&#010;&gt; &gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; phase bindings.  And, if you have a more complex sequence with 3&#010;&gt; &gt; plugins&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; and multiple executions of each, there aren't enough available&#010;&gt; &gt; phases to&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; successfully order everything.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; It should be possible to bind multiple plugin executions, of&#010;&gt; &gt; DIFFERENT&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; plugins, to a single phase and deterministically specify the&#010;&gt; &gt; execution&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; order.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Sorry, I disagree.  One alternative is to use antrun, but that seems like&#010;&gt; going backwards.  I'm really curious why there's a strong philosophical&#010;&gt; objection to requesting this enhancement.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Is it unreasonable to suggest that "The Maven Way" is not perfect and&#010;&gt; might need some adjustments to handle common use-cases the original&#010;&gt; designers didn't foresee?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Is my goal of using Maven to automate CI/CD, which can involve configuring&#010;&gt; external resources by running various plugins in a specific sequence,&#010;&gt; somehow in violation of "the Maven way"?&#010;&#010;&#010;See I just knew it was going to be something like deploying to multiple&#010;environments or other things that are outside the standard lifecycle...&#010;&#010;So let's take a step back and see if you are actually hacking the standard&#010;lifecycle to do something outside of its original intended use case?&#010;&#010;Are you doing things that should happen before publishing the artifacts to&#010;a remote repository or after publishing? (And try to forget how you think&#010;maven should work, rather look at the higher level)&#010;&#010;Publishing to a remote repository is allowing others to consume the&#010;artifact as is, without changing it.&#010;&#010;Are you reconfiguring the artifact for use in different environments? (That&#010;should better be a separate customisation module that consumes the&#010;previously published artifact)&#010;&#010;I have yet to see a genuine use case where a refactoring leads to a better&#010;build process and remove the need to do multiple things in the same&#010;phase... Ever case I have seen is either a refactoring to multiple modules&#010;or writing a plugin to perform the complex sequence of steps for a specific&#010;*class* of artifact where multiple of this class of artifacts is required&#010;(ie the write a plugin solution)&#010;&#010;Usually the root cause is people trying to make their builds overly complex.&#010;&#010;If you are doing maven right you should only have the packaging,&#010;dependencies and a build extension in you pom (yes slight hyperbole here,&#010;but think of this as the ideal)&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; Consider the phrase "...you have wandered off The Maven Way™".  I can't&#010;&gt; tell if you intended this ironically or seriously.  If it's the latter, it&#010;&gt; seems like you're saying is "Maven is perfect. If Maven doesn't handle your&#010;&gt; use-case, then your use-case is invalid".  Is that true?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Nope maven is far from perfect. Plugins are the path to that perfection&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Sent from my phone&#010;&#010;

On Wed, Jun 4, 2014 at 12:08 PM, Jim Garrison &lt;jim.garrison@nwea.org&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Consider the phrase "...you have wandered off The Maven Way™".  I can't&#010;&gt; tell if you intended this ironically or seriously.  If it's the latter, it&#010;&gt; seems like you're saying is "Maven is perfect. If Maven doesn't handle your&#010;&gt; use-case, then your use-case is invalid".  Is that true?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Just observing this conversation.  The so-called Maven Way™ can probably be&#010;reduced to: favor new plugins over more XML in your pom.xml files.&#010;&#010;I think (my interpretation only; this and $4 will get you a cup of coffee)&#010;this is because at least originally—and for what it's worth it still seems&#010;this way to me—your pom.xml is supposed to be a declarative object model.&#010; It's not really a place for stitching together plugin executions.  The&#010;thinking is (again, for better or worse; don't shoot the messenger) that if&#010;you have some sequence of events that must take place at a particular point&#010;in the lifecycle, then encapsulate that sequence of events into a plugin&#010;and bind it once.&#010;&#010;Of course that presupposes a certain amount of ease-of-software-reuse in&#010;the plugin ecosystem—i.e. that it's brain-dead simple to write a plugin&#010;that combines other plugins—which may or may not actually be true depending&#010;on how the to-be-combined plugins were actually authored.&#010;&#010;Best,&#010;Laird&#010;&#010;-- &#010;http://about.me/lairdnelson&#010;&#010;

On Wednesday, 4 June 2014, Jason van Zyl &lt;jason@takari.io&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; On Jun 4, 2014, at 12:07 PM, Stephen Connolly &lt;&#010;&gt; stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com &lt;javascript:;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; That's usually a sign that you have wandered off The Maven Way™&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; No it's not. They have valid points and the implementation is deficient in&#010;&gt; this regard. Everything that's presently here is not immutable. Calling it&#010;&gt; "The Maven Way" doesn't make it usable or without flaws. I'm not even sure&#010;&gt; where this saying came from but we're not a cult.&#010;&#010;&#010;I use the term "The Maven Way" to mean "the established best practice way&#010;to build an XYZ"...&#010;&#010;So when I say you have wandered off the Maven way, I mean that you are&#010;encountering fractions because of your choice.&#010;&#010;Why have you wandered off the conventional path? Probably because it does&#010;not fit your needs.&#010;&#010;If this is a once off, never to be repeated, thing... Well you can live&#010;with the hacks you use to make it work...&#010;&#010;Otherwise a new plugin with the required packaging type and a mojo to do&#010;the "complex thing" in one single step is a much better solution...&#010;&#010;And now in doing that you have forged a new Maven way... If you contribute&#010;that way back to the community then our community grows richer because of&#010;your efforts forging a new oath through the wild jungle.&#010;&#010;There are four or five paths established and maintained by the maven&#010;project:&#010;&#010;* simple jar&#010;* simple war&#010;* simple ear&#010;* simple ejb-jar&#010;* simple rar&#010;&#010;Are our paths perfect? Nope... For one our war path is not well adapted to&#010;modern web application development... But it is still unclear the best path&#010;to follow for modern war artifacts... I have an open experiment (jszip.org)&#010;there's the webjars effort, etc&#010;&#010;Somebody will find a *great path* for modern war files... Then if they can&#010;get that into a packaging (bonus if the maven-war-plugin) the community can&#010;all rejoice in the simplified new path and our poms can return to just&#010;listing dependencies&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; There are ways back onto the blessed path... they typically involve&#010;&gt; writing&#010;&gt; &gt; a plugin&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Jason&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ----------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; Jason van Zyl&#010;&gt; Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;&gt; http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;&gt; http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I never make the mistake of arguing with people for whose opinions I have&#010;&gt; no respect.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -- Edward Gibbon&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Sent from my phone&#010;&#010;

I, myself, have also found the lack of ordered plugin execution to be&#010;wanting. Stephen does have a point: complex behavior is likely be better&#010;encapsulated in a new plugin. I don't disagree, but that route can be steep&#010;and I don't want to be detoured into always writing a new plugin. Many&#010;times such behavior can be emulated simply by aggregating the use of&#010;plugins in an ordered fashion. For example, one plugin executes a SQL&#010;script to setup a database, the next plugin executes a Java program to&#010;populate the database according to logic. I've tried that before and can't&#010;because such plugin ordering doesn't exist. For example, one plugin executes a SQL&#010;&gt; &gt; script to setup a database, the next plugin executes a Java program to&#010;&gt; &gt; populate the database according to logic.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Ahem  http://flywaydb.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I've tried that before and can't&#010;&gt; &gt; because such plugin ordering doesn't exist. So if there is an easy way to&#010;&gt; &gt; bring this minor enhancement to the Maven community, in 3.x, I think we&#010;&gt; &gt; should.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt; &gt; Paul&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; On Wed, Jun 4, 2014 at 3:08 PM, Ron Wheeler &lt;&#010;&gt; &gt; rwheeler@artifact-software.com &lt;javascript:;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; "We are not a cult."&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; If we already have a "we", we are half way there!&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Just short a charismatic leader and a "Book of the Way".&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Ron&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; On 04/06/2014 3:22 PM, Jason van Zyl wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; On Jun 4, 2014, at 12:07 PM, Stephen Connolly &lt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com &lt;javascript:;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;  That's usually a sign that you have wandered off The Maven Way™&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;  No it's not. They have valid points and the implementation is&#010;&gt; &gt; deficient&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; in this regard. Everything that's presently here is not immutable.&#010;&gt; &gt; Calling&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt; it "The Maven Way" doesn't make it usable or without flaws. Fri, 06 Jun 2014 21:23:05 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;flatten-maven-plugin version 1.0.0-beta-2.&#010;&#010;Flatten Maven Plugin generates a flattened version of your pom.xml and &#010;makes maven to install&#010;and deploy this one instead of the original pom.xml.&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/flatten-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin &#010;configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;         &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;         &lt;artifactId&gt;flatten-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;         &lt;version&gt;1.0.0-beta-2&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;All you need to do is add the plugin to the plugins in your build section.&#010;&#010;Release Notes&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MOJO-2027 ability to preserve developer &#010;information&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MOJO-2030 flatten-maven-plugin overrides &#010;basedir and sets it to target/, so src/site/site.xml is not used and any &#010;documentation beneath src/site is not rendered&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Ben Podgursky &lt;bpodgur...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Concurrent maven processes using the same repository failing when new snapshot version downloaded  
Date  :-
Wed, 11 Jun 2014 00:27:22 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi all,&#010;&#010;I'm running into a problem where maven processes using a shared repository&#010;are getting exceptions when a new snapshot dependency is deployed.  Our&#010;setup is:&#010;&#010;- We use Jenkins continuous integration builds.  The builds are just&#010;running a simple "mvn clean deploy".&#010;- Our build machines often run builds for two projects simultaneously.&#010; When running simultaneously, the builds will share a maven respository.&#010;&#010;We have (for simplification) three projects A, B, and C.  Each of these is&#010;deployed as a snapshot at the end of a successful build.  Projects B and C&#010;each depend on a snapshot version of of project A.&#010;&#010;Intermittently, when projects B and C are running simultaneously on a&#010;machine, the build which started first will begin to fail all tests with&#010;java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError, where the classes not found belong to&#010;project A.  I've verified that the classfiles are present in A's deployed&#010;jar.&#010;&#010;I *believe* what is happening is:&#010;&#010;1) project B begins building, and starts surefire tests.&#010;2) project A deploys a new snapshot version (possibly from a different&#010;machine)&#010;3) project C begings building.  Because our snapshot update policy is set&#010;to "always", it downloads the new version of "A-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar", and&#010;replaces the previous version in the local respository&#010;4) the tests for project B start to fail because they are using a reference&#010;to a file which has been deleted&#010;&#010;I've looked into what surefire is putting on the classpath, and even though&#010;the repository has the specific version of the snapshot available, (ex&#010;"A-1.0-20140610.213850-369.jar"), it's putting&#010;"analysis_lib-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar" on the classpath.  I don't understand why&#010;maven would prefer to use the artifact which could get replaced rather than&#010;the semi-permanent artifact (I understand snapshot versions aren't&#010;permanent, but it would at least survive for the duration of the build.)&#010;&#010;My questions are:&#010;&#010;- does this sequence of events seem plausible, or is there another&#010;explanation to the exceptions I'm seeing?&#010;&#010;- is there a way I can force maven to put the timestamped version of&#010;artifacts on the classpath instead of the SNAPSHOT versions?  I understand&#010;I can specify the timestamp in the pom.xml, but that's not what I want--I&#010;just want it to choose the current version when the build starts, and use&#010;that for the duration of the build.  I'm also familiar with mvn&#010;versions:lock-snapshots, but I'd rather avoid it if possible because (1) it&#010;adds build complexity and (2) it doesn't lock versions pulled in&#010;transitively (ex D -&gt; A -&gt; B, if D was a snapshot), since I don't want to&#010;deploy artifacts with locked versions&#010;&#010;&#010;Thanks for your time,&#010;&#010;Ben&#010;&#010;  

================

Re: Concurrent maven processes using the same repository failing when new snapshot version downloaded  
Date  :-
Wed, 11 Jun 2014 21:45:00 GMT  
contents:- 
After a bit of hunting, it turns out Jenkins has an option under "Manage&#010;Jenkins" -&gt; "Configure System" -&gt; "Maven Project Configuration" -&gt; "Local&#010;Maven Repository" -&gt; "Local to the executor" which will use an isolated&#010;repository for each executor process, which solves this pretty cleanly.&#010; Thanks for the tip.&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Jun 11, 2014 at 1:24 AM, Ben Podgursky &lt;bpodgursky@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks Kristian, I'll check that out.  Are there any tickets I could&#010;&gt; follow to keep an eye out for the fix?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Tue, Jun 10, 2014 at 10:55 PM, Kristian Rosenvold &lt;&#010;&gt; kristian.rosenvold@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; This is a known problem (old one), which might actaully be getting a&#010;&gt;&gt; fix "soon". In the meantime, checkout&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; http://blog.sonatype.com/2009/01/maven-continuous-integration-best-practices/&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Kristian&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 2014-06-11 2:27 GMT+02:00 Ben Podgursky &lt;bpodgursky@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; I'm running into a problem where maven processes using a shared&#010;&gt;&gt; repository&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; are getting exceptions when a new snapshot dependency is deployed. The builds are just&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; running a simple "mvn clean deploy".&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; - Our build machines often run builds for two projects simultaneously.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;  When running simultaneously, the builds will share a maven respository.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; We have (for simplification) three projects A, B, and C. Projects B&#010;&gt;&gt; and C&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; each depend on a snapshot version of of project A.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Intermittently, when projects B and C are running simultaneously on a&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; machine, the build which started first will begin to fail all tests with&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError, where the classes not found belong to&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; project A.  I've verified that the classfiles are present in A's&#010;&gt;&gt; deployed&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; jar.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; I *believe* what is happening is:&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; 1) project B begins building, and starts surefire tests.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; 2) project A deploys a new snapshot version (possibly from a different&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; machine)&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; 3) project C begings building.  Because our snapshot update policy is&#010;&gt;&gt; set&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; to "always", it downloads the new version of "A-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar", and&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; replaces the previous version in the local respository&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; 4) the tests for project B start to fail because they are using a&#010;&gt;&gt; reference&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; to a file which has been deleted&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; I've looked into what surefire is putting on the classpath, and even&#010;&gt;&gt; though&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; the repository has the specific version of the snapshot available, (ex&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; "A-1.0-20140610.213850-369.jar"), it's putting&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; "analysis_lib-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar" on the classpath.  I don't understand&#010;&gt;&gt; why&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; maven would prefer to use the artifact which could get replaced rather&#010;&gt;&gt; than&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; the semi-permanent artifact (I understand snapshot versions aren't&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; permanent, but it would at least survive for the duration of the build.)&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; My questions are:&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; - does this sequence of events seem plausible, or is there another&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; explanation to the exceptions I'm seeing?&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; - is there a way I can force maven to put the timestamped version of&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; artifacts on the classpath instead of the SNAPSHOT versions?  I&#010;&gt;&gt; understand&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; I can specify the timestamp in the pom.xml, but that's not what I&#010;&gt;&gt; want--I&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; just want it to choose the current version when the build starts, and&#010;&gt;&gt; use&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; that for the duration of the build.  I'm also familiar with mvn&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; versions:lock-snapshots, but I'd rather avoid it if possible because&#010;&gt;&gt; (1) it&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; adds build complexity and (2) it doesn't lock versions pulled in&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; transitively (ex D -&gt; A -&gt; B, if D was a snapshot), since I don't want&#010;&gt;&gt; to&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; deploy artifacts with locked versions&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Thanks for your time,&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Ben&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Ron Wheeler &lt;rwhee...@artifact-software.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: How to reference a multimodule project from a pom  
Date  :-
Wed, 11 Jun 2014 23:52:13 GMT  
contents:- 
Yes.&#010;We have given these jars the name "aggregation jars".&#010;You add a 6th project that produces a jar containing the 5 "real" jars &#010;and have your projects reference the aggregation jar.&#010;&#010;Others have used the term "bundle" for this (Apache CXF)  but that may &#010;confuse people who have OSGI "bundles" in mind.&#010;&#010;http://blog.artifact-software.com/tech/?p=121 is a short article on what &#010;we do and why.&#010;You might want to look at other notes that we have tagged with "Maven" &#010;as well.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 11/06/2014 12:08 PM, kurt_cobain wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi, I have a multimodule project, let's call it "multi". it generates like 5&#010;&gt; jar artifacts.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I would like to simply reference "multi" from another project's pom and get&#010;&gt; everything i need, without having to indivdivually reference each of the 5&#010;&gt; jar's generated by "multi" in my the referencing pom file.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Isn't that possible?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/How-to-reference-a-multimodule-project-from-a-pom-tp5795419.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hello everyone, :)&#010;&#010;okay, I tried a different approach:&#010;&#010;Instead of that &lt;configuration&gt; section in the settings.xml I copied my&#010;local know_hosts file from&#010;&#009;C:\Users\[MY_USER]\.ssh\known_hosts&#010;to the server:&#010;&#009;C:\Windows\system32\config\.ssh\known_hosts&#010;I read in the Internet that this folder is the folder of the system&#010;account which is used e.g. by Tomcat.&#010;And as Jenkins and Maven are executed by Tomcat, they should work on the&#010;same folder.&#010;&#010;Unfortunately I didn't work: I see in the Jenkins Build log that&#010;wagon-ssh keeps asking if it should trust the connection by showing the&#010;SSH RSA fingerprint. Unfortunately wagon-ssh also doesn't show at which&#010;location it tries to open the known_hosts file.&#010;&#010;The easiest way would be if I would be able to specify the path of the&#010;known_hosts file in the settings.xml. But I haven't found anything about&#010;a configuration parameter like that.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Gerrit&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi Gerrit,&#010;&#010;&gt; I see in the Jenkins Build log that wagon-ssh keeps asking if it&#010;&gt; should trust the connection by showing the SSH RSA fingerprint.&#010;&#010;Maybe your Jenkins's %USER_HOME% is simply not set as you expect?&#010;Apparently [2], Jenkins on Windows defaults to C:\Users\[MY_USER]\.jenkins,&#010;so maybe you need to put your known_hosts in&#010;C:\Users\[MY_USER]\.jenkins\.ssh\known_hosts in order for it to run&#010;properly with Jenkins?&#010;&#010;&gt; The easiest way would be if I would be able to specify the path of the&#010;&gt; known_hosts file in the settings.xml.&#010;&#010;Looking at the relevant maven-wagon source [1], it is clear there is a&#010;bunch of logic for managing a KnownHostsProvider (which controls where the&#010;known_hosts data comes from). So I would be very surprised if this was not&#010;exposed at the Maven level -- i.e., if there was not a way to configure&#010;this in the POM somehow.&#010;&#010;&gt; Unfortunately wagon-ssh also doesn't show at which location it tries&#010;&gt; to open the known_hosts file.&#010;&#010;Did you try with "mvn -X"? That is verbose/debug mode. If it still doesn't&#010;echo the path, please file a JIRA issue for it:&#010;https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/WAGON (create account at&#010;https://xircles.codehaus.org/signup)&#010;&#010;&gt; Does no one of you use that wagon-ssh?&#010;&#010;My group uses wagon-webdav-jackrabbit for artifact deploys, and we aren't&#010;deploying our Maven sites properly yet.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;[1]&#010;https://github.com/apache/maven-wagon/blob/41336732524e33fa3fdc99f07b6add013b23dfa7/wagon-providers/wagon-ssh/src/main/java/org/apache/maven/wagon/providers/ssh/jsch/AbstractJschWagon.java#L89&#010;&#010;[2] http://stackoverflow.com/q/12689139&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Jun 24, 2014 at 6:42 AM, Hohl, Gerrit &lt;g.hohl@aurenz.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello everyone,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I still having this problem. So I would be very surprised if this &#013;&#010;&gt; was not exposed at the Maven level -- i.e., if there was not a way to &#013;&#010;&gt; configure this in the POM somehow.&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; Unfortunately wagon-ssh also doesn't show at which location it tries &#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; to open the known_hosts file.&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; Did you try with "mvn -X"? That is verbose/debug mode. If it still &#013;&#010;&gt; doesn't echo the path, please file a JIRA issue for it:&#013;&#010;&gt; https://jira.codehaus.org/browse/WAGON (create account at&#013;&#010;&gt; https://xircles.codehaus.org/signup)&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; Does no one of you use that wagon-ssh?&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; My group uses wagon-webdav-jackrabbit for artifact deploys, and we &#013;&#010;&gt; aren't deploying our Maven sites properly yet.&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#013;&#010;&gt; Curtis&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; [1]&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; https://github.com/apache/maven-wagon/blob/41336732524e33fa3fdc99f07b6&#013;&#010;&gt; add013b23dfa7/wagon-providers/wagon-ssh/src/main/java/org/apache/maven&#013;&#010;&gt; /wagon/providers/ssh/jsch/AbstractJschWagon.java#L89&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; [2] http://stackoverflow.com/q/12689139&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; On Tue, Jun 24, 2014 at 6:42 AM, Hohl, Gerrit &lt;g.hohl@aurenz.de&gt; wrote:&#013;&#010;&gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hello everyone,&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#013;&#010;&gt; &gt; I still having this problem. &quot;Hohl, Gerrit&quot; &lt;g.h...@aurenz.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
Complex Maven projects - Tutorials? Books?  
Date  :-
Thu, 12 Jun 2014 08:44:57 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello everyone, :)&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;I have a question which is not about a specific problem with Maven, but&#010;more a general question.&#010;&#010;I hope it is okay to ask this question here.&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;We use Maven and Jenkins for about 1.5 years now, I guess. Until now the&#010;Maven projects have been very simple and - let's say - very monolithic.&#010;&#010;But recently we identify more and more internal libraries in our&#010;products. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by&#010;copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&#010;So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. But&#010;most of them only deal with simple projects. They don't cover e.g.&#010;versioning the build process (especially if your build process consists&#010;of more than just one step). They also don't cover the problems of&#010;developing the libraries while your developing the products which depend&#010;on them. Especially at the beginning your libraries will go through a&#010;lot of changes. A few name snapshots as a solution, but don't explain&#010;how you can work using them, how you can use them in your pom.xml and&#010;how you deal with them if you finally switch your product and/or your&#010;library from the snapshot state to the release state. A few also say&#010;that you shouldn't use snapshots at all because it will result in many&#010;problems (e.g. having -SNAPSHOT entries in your pom.xml). Nightly builds&#010;or build triggered by the SCM are also an issue here.&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these&#010;issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Gerrit&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;&#010;  

================

Hello everyone, :)&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;I have a question which is not about a specific problem with Maven, but&#010;more a general question.&#010;&#010;I hope it is okay to ask this question here.&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;We use Maven and Jenkins for about 1.5 years now, I guess. Until now the&#010;Maven projects have been very simple and - let's say - very monolithic.&#010;&#010;But recently we identify more and more internal libraries in our&#010;products. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by&#010;copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&#010;So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. But&#010;most of them only deal with simple projects. They don't cover e.g.&#010;versioning the build process (especially if your build process consists&#010;of more than just one step). They also don't cover the problems of&#010;developing the libraries while your developing the products which depend&#010;on them. Especially at the beginning your libraries will go through a&#010;lot of changes. A few name snapshots as a solution, but don't explain&#010;how you can work using them, how you can use them in your pom.xml and&#010;how you deal with them if you finally switch your product and/or your&#010;library from the snapshot state to the release state. A few also say&#010;that you shouldn't use snapshots at all because it will result in many&#010;problems (e.g. having -SNAPSHOT entries in your pom.xml). Nightly builds&#010;or build triggered by the SCM are also an issue here.&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these&#010;issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Gerrit&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Michael Osipov &lt;micha...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Complex Maven projects - Tutorials? Books?  
Date  :-
Thu, 12 Jun 2014 18:39:13 GMT  
contents:- 
Am 2014-06-12 16:46, schrieb Hohl, Gerrit:&#010;&gt; Hello everyone, :)&#010;[..]&#010;&gt; Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these&#010;&gt; issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&#010;Hi Gerrit,&#010;&#010;here is the approach I have been using all the years, I think this is &#010;quite common in companies:&#010;&#010;1. Set up a Nexus instance in your company, mirroring Central and with &#010;release/snapshot repos for your company.&#010;&#010;1.1 Make sure that Nexus works correctly.&#010;&#010;2. Let the CI server deploy SNAPSHOTs of you libraries deploy to your &#010;Nexus instance frequently.&#010;&#010;3. Refer to those SNAPSHOTs in your project POMs if you need bleeding &#010;edge. This makes it easier to soak in fixed bugs in deps. If you think &#010;that your lib is stable enough, release to SCM and Nexus.&#010;&#010;4. Use the maven-versions-plugin to update your project dependencies and &#010;or fix to a release version.&#010;&#010;It is perfectly fine to rely on SNAPSHOTs during development but not &#010;when you perform mvn release:prepare release:perform.&#010;&#010;Gruß,&#010;&#010;Michael&#010;&#010;PS: Upgrade your Maven version to a new one if you are able to.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Great advice.&#010;We depend on Nexus.&#010;If you are serious about Maven, you need a repo.&#010;The community version of Nexus is a great benefit to the Maven community.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 12/06/2014 2:39 PM, Michael Osipov wrote:&#010;&gt; Am 2014-06-12 16:46, schrieb Hohl, Gerrit:&#010;&gt;&gt; Hello everyone, :)&#010;&gt; [..]&#010;&gt;&gt; Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these&#010;&gt;&gt; issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hi Gerrit,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; here is the approach I have been using all the years, I think this is &#010;&gt; quite common in companies:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1. Set up a Nexus instance in your company, mirroring Central and with &#010;&gt; release/snapshot repos for your company.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 1.1 Make sure that Nexus works correctly.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 2. Let the CI server deploy SNAPSHOTs of you libraries deploy to your &#010;&gt; Nexus instance frequently.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 3. Refer to those SNAPSHOTs in your project POMs if you need bleeding &#010;&gt; edge. This makes it easier to soak in fixed bugs in deps. If you think &#010;&gt; that your lib is stable enough, release to SCM and Nexus.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; 4. Good questions.&#010;I have never heard anything negative about SNAPSHOTs from those who use &#010;them.&#010;&#010;Notice - Free advice:&#010;- Separate your utilities from your applications. If they have a life of &#010;their own, you can manage the dependencies more easily.&#010;- Test your utilities and libraries separately. Use SNAPSHOTs and a &#010;release process that is separate from your application.&#010;- Have your applications treat your utilities and libraries as if they &#010;were written by some other organization.&#010;- Use dependency management in the parent POM to control versions of &#010;utilities. This gives you one place to maintain the versions.&#010;End of free advice.&#010;&#010;Free commentary.&#010;At the beginning, you are correct, it will be harder to provide a stable &#010;environment but that is where SNAPSHOTs are a big help.&#010;Version 2.1.0-SHAPSHOT of the application depends on version &#010;1.0-SNAPSHOT of file-manager-core until file-manager-core stabilizes and &#010;becomes version 1.0.  Generally speaking, the application should still &#010;be a SNAPSHOT after your utilities become releases since you should be &#010;able to stabilize the functionality and finish the testing of the &#010;utilities before the same can happen to the application modules.&#010;End of fee commentary&#010;&#010;I think that you will find this advice at least worth the cost and you &#010;may get some comments from the smarter and more knowledgeable people &#010;here that refines or contradicts my advice.&#010;&#010;There is lots of good Maven information freely available and lots of &#010;projects that are very complex being developed with Maven.&#010;Our biggest project had over 70 Maven modules of which 10 where &#010;supporting libraries either written by us or aggregated from existing &#010;open source projects.&#010;&#010;We have some articles describing how we use Maven in our technical blog &#010;at http://blog.artifact-software.com/tech.&#010;Jokes are found at http://blog.artifact-software.com/fun if you need a &#010;smile to face the world of Maven.&#010;&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 12/06/2014 10:46 AM, Hohl, Gerrit wrote:&#010;&gt; Hello everyone, :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have a question which is not about a specific problem with Maven, but&#010;&gt; more a general question.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I hope it is okay to ask this question here.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We use Maven and Jenkins for about 1.5 years now, I guess. Until now the&#010;&gt; Maven projects have been very simple and - let's say - very monolithic.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But recently we identify more and more internal libraries in our&#010;&gt; products. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by&#010;&gt; copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. But&#010;&gt; most of them only deal with simple projects. They don't cover e.g.&#010;&gt; versioning the build process (especially if your build process consists&#010;&gt; of more than just one step). They also don't cover the problems of&#010;&gt; developing the libraries while your developing the products which depend&#010;&gt; on them. Especially at the beginning your libraries will go through a&#010;&gt; lot of changes. A few name snapshots as a solution, but don't explain&#010;&gt; how you can work using them, how you can use them in your pom.xml and&#010;&gt; how you deal with them if you finally switch your product and/or your&#010;&gt; library from the snapshot state to the release state. A few also say&#010;&gt; that you shouldn't use snapshots at all because it will result in many&#010;&gt; problems (e.g. having -SNAPSHOT entries in your pom.xml). Nightly builds&#010;&gt; or build triggered by the SCM are also an issue here.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these&#010;&gt; issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Gerrit&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

On 13 June 2014 00:16, Hohl, Gerrit &lt;g.hohl@aurenz.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; We use Maven and Jenkins for about 1.5 years now, I guess. Until now the&#010;&gt; Maven projects have been very simple and - let's say - very monolithic.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But recently we identify more and more internal libraries in our&#010;&gt; products. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by&#010;&gt; copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. But&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Can you list what you've read so far?&#010;I assume you've gone through the ones we link at the Maven site?&#010;http://maven.apache.org/articles.html&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; most of them only deal with simple projects. They don't cover e.g.&#010;&gt; versioning the build process (especially if your build process consists&#010;&gt; of more than just one step). They also don't cover the problems of&#010;&gt; developing the libraries while your developing the products which depend&#010;&gt; on them. Especially at the beginning your libraries will go through a&#010;&gt; lot of changes. A few name snapshots as a solution, but don't explain&#010;&gt; how you can work using them, how you can use them in your pom.xml and&#010;&gt; how you deal with them if you finally switch your product and/or your&#010;&gt; library from the snapshot state to the release state. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by&#010;&gt; &gt; copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. A few name snapshots as a solution, but don't explain&#010;&gt; &gt; how you can work using them, how you can use them in your pom.xml and&#010;&gt; &gt; how you deal with them if you finally switch your product and/or your&#010;&gt; &gt; library from the snapshot state to the release state. There were usually two books&#010;&gt; for any product:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; o  Reference Manual -- *complete* individual descriptions of each feature,&#010;&gt;     command, and qualifier.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; o  Programmer's (or User's) Guide -- fits all the pieces together and&#010;&gt;     suggests good ways to think about the facility under discussion.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I typically had both open when working on anything nontrivial. Explanations are rarely more than a statement of &#010;the obvious (Property: enabled:  true/false - enable or disable &#010;feature).  The question of WHY is rarely addressed and downstream &#010;results never.  Even if you do find a well detailed example it is very &#010;specific (cookbook style) with little explanation of the options NOT &#010;chosen and why.&#010;&#010;I'm running into this right now in fact. With a configuration &#010;file like XML which is designed to ignore options it doesn't understand, &#010;this is even more frustrating.  With rapidly  changing feature sets it's &#010;maddening.&#010;&#010;Actually having access to OLD documentation would help understand the &#010;difference between the "old but still supported" vs. the "shiny, new &#010;preferred" way.  I still have not found a good discussion about the &#010;difference between using the POM reporting section and adding reporting &#010;plugins to the maven-site-plugin in the build section. All I know at the &#010;moment is more plugins seemed to work as I expected when adding the &#010;plugins to the maven-site-plugin in the build section than when trying &#010;to add them to the reporting section.&#010;&#010;For whatever reason, my career has been one of trouble shooting, proof &#010;of concept and other, very targeted activities. My &#010;efforts historically rely on being clever, persistent and willing to buy &#010;every book I can find on the subject. Generally, the modern JavaDoc &#010;mentality of documentation blows.  If I want to read the source code &#010;(and I can) I'll write the source code (which I can). It will also help future&#010;projects at your org.&#010;&#010;Actually having access to OLD documentation would help understand the&#010;&gt; difference between the "old but still supported" vs. the "shiny, new&#010;&gt; preferred" way.&#010;&#010;&#010;The previous plugin docs are always available they are versioned on the&#010;website.&#010;But they are unlikely to discuss why things were changed.&#010;You might get lucky and find that information in the jira changeset.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; I still have not found a good discussion about the difference between&#010;&gt; using the POM reporting section and adding reporting plugins to the&#010;&gt; maven-site-plugin in the build section. If you are really aiming at doing continuous delivery (any potential &#010;build can be pushed to prod), then SNAPSHOT is not a great way to deal &#010;with dependencies since you will not be able to exactly know what you &#010;ship. To avoid this, one practice is to use the build number in the &#010;artifact version (1.0.0-b1 or 1.0.1).&#010;This has of course had the drawback that now you have to update the &#010;pom.xml of components using a specific artifact (move from build 1 to 2) &#010;but this also gives you greater control on the rate at which you consume &#010;libraries.&#010;You may be interested in these articles:&#010;- &#010;http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Continuous-Delivery-and-Maven-td3245370.html&#010;- &#010;http://stackoverflow.com/questions/18456111/what-is-the-maven-way-for-project-versions-when-doing-continuous-delivery&#010;&#010;That said, if you add Artifactory to the mix, you can leverage its &#010;capabilities of obtaining specific versions of a SNAPSHOT through matrix &#010;parameters &#010;(https://www.jfrog.com/confluence/display/RTF/Using+Properties+in+Deployment+and+Resolution)&#010;&#010;quite handy. One example where this comes handy is when you split your &#010;build process over multiple jenkins jobs and you want to make sure that &#010;you use the same artifact throughout the process and this w/o blocking &#010;the whole "pipeline" for the whole duration of the process.&#010;&#010;HTH&#010;&#010;Pascal&#010;On 12/06/2014 10:46 AM, Hohl, Gerrit wrote:&#010;&gt; Hello everyone, :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have a question which is not about a specific problem with Maven, but&#010;&gt; more a general question.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I hope it is okay to ask this question here.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We use Maven and Jenkins for about 1.5 years now, I guess. Until now the&#010;&gt; Maven projects have been very simple and - let's say - very monolithic.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But recently we identify more and more internal libraries in our&#010;&gt; products. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by&#010;&gt; copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. But&#010;&gt; most of them only deal with simple projects. They don't cover e.g.&#010;&gt; versioning the build process (especially if your build process consists&#010;&gt; of more than just one step). They also don't cover the problems of&#010;&gt; developing the libraries while your developing the products which depend&#010;&gt; on them. Especially at the beginning your libraries will go through a&#010;&gt; lot of changes. A few name snapshots as a solution, but don't explain&#010;&gt; how you can work using them, how you can use them in your pom.xml and&#010;&gt; how you deal with them if you finally switch your product and/or your&#010;&gt; library from the snapshot state to the release state. A few also say&#010;&gt; that you shouldn't use snapshots at all because it will result in many&#010;&gt; problems (e.g. having -SNAPSHOT entries in your pom.xml). Nightly builds&#010;&gt; or build triggered by the SCM are also an issue here.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these&#010;&gt; issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Gerrit&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;
