Name  :- 
&quot;Hohl, Gerrit&quot; &lt;g.h...@aurenz.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
AW: Complex Maven projects - Tutorials? Books?  
Date  :-
Fri, 13 Jun 2014 08:41:53 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello everyone, :)&#010;&#010;wow, I got a lot of useful responses. Thanks a lot, Michael, Ron, Barrie and Pascal.&#010;And sorry for the double mail. Seems the mailing list got it twice.&#010;&#010;We already have a Nexus running here (v2.6.2-01 - I know: There is v2.8.1-01 available) and&#010;use it as a mirror / proxy as well as for uploading some JAR and POM files which are not available&#010;in the public repositories.&#010;&#010;Instead of the Maven Versions Plugin we came across the Maven Release Plugin. This way you&#010;can check in all the time, but only once the build process creates a stable release by modifying&#010;the pom.xml files, building, checking in this version of the pom.xml into the SCM, tagging&#010;or branching this version in the SCM, modifying the pom.xml again (back to snaphots) and checking&#010;it in again.&#010;But we asked ourselves if this is really the best solution as it seemed a little bit complex&#010;and if there isn't a more simple solution for doing that.&#010;I have to admit that a colleague was working on that issue and not me. I will discuss it with&#010;him again.&#010;&#010;Another colleague and I said the same like Ron wrote. That internal libraries should be handled&#010;like external ones.&#010;Our problem at the moment is that the libraries as well as the application change every day.&#010;We don't have separated teams for applications and libraries - we are too small for that.&#010;On the other side other developers of the team have to rely on changes which are made. So&#010;we have to publish them to the SCM. Here we face the problem that we also have to deploy them&#010;to Nexus as the other party maybe only works on one project, but doesn't have the library&#010;checked out from the SCM at the same time. So if project A is checked in you also have to&#010;deploy library B. Otherwise the other developer which checks out project A won't be able to&#010;start it, maybe even to compile it, because project A in the SCM depends on a newer library&#010;B version than the developer has in his local repository.&#010;My argument in the discussion back then was that this should be solved by snapshots. Especially&#010;if you have a build server which is triggered by changes in the SCM you would be able to have&#010;the newest version of the library always available in your Nexus repository.&#010;&#010;We read many articles on the Internet so far. And we read the following books:&#010;&#010;Maven 2 - Eine Einführung, aktuell zur Version 2.0.9 (Maven 2 - An introduction)&#010;Author: Kai Uwe Bachmann&#010;Publisher: Addision-Wesley&#010;ISBN: 978-3-8273-2835-9&#010;It is a really only an introduction and many things are not mentioned or discusses in that&#010;book. Kai talks only about very simply examples. He doesn't write about more complex problems&#010;you will face for sure if you work a little bit longer and maybe on bigger projects using&#010;Maven.&#010;&#010;Jenkins - kurz &amp; gut&#010;Author: Mario Behrendt&#010;Publisher: O'Reilly&#010;ISBN: 978-3-86899-127-7&#010;This books is not directly related to Maven, but also mentions it. It is a short overview&#010;of CI using Jenkins. I guess you won't get Jenkins running if you only read this book. But&#010;maybe it is a good help for making a decision if you want to use Jenkins or not.&#010;&#010;Jenkins - The Definitive Guide&#010;Author: John Ferguson Smart&#010;Publisher: O'Reilly&#010;ISBN: 978-1-449-30535-2&#010;Also not directly related to Maven, but explain how to use Jenkins and Maven together.&#010;&#010;I also bought recently:&#010;Continuous Delivery: Reliable Software Releases Through Build, Test, and Deployment Automation&#010;Authors: Jez Humble, David Farley&#010;Publisher: Addision-Wesley&#010;ISBN: 978-0321601919&#010;I haven't read it yet. But I hope to get a deeper understanding of the whole process. But&#010;I'm not sure if it will help me solving our problems.&#010;&#010;I had a look on the books on the Maven site. Most look like they are already old and dealing&#010;with Maven 2 (like the book we have - unfortunately - also does). And the newest one got some&#010;poor reviews (okay, they are subjective, so maybe the book isn't that bad). Maybe one of you&#010;can give a recommendation for a book which is not dedicated to beginners, but instead handles&#010;some issues of developers who are already on the next level (but not on the highest level&#010;yet).&#010;&#010;Of course we are also reading the online documentation. But I have to admit that it sometimes&#010;lacks the one or another information which you find in some blogs or articles after some search.&#010;And some of the 3rd party plugins are explained really poorly (okay, that is not a problem&#010;of the Maven project). That doesn't make it easier as Maven offers some many possibilities&#010;and therefore *can* get complex.&#010;&#010;We also found a presentation on the Internet which described a solution like Pascal mentioned&#010;in his mail. But doesn't that mean that you will have hundreds and hundreds of releases in&#010;your repository? And doesn't it mean you have to update the pom.xml files of your projects&#010;which are developed simultaneously all the time? Somehow I prefer the idea - like Ron - of&#010;handling internal libraries not different from external libraries. But I also see the points&#010;of people who argument for the CD way-of-life.&#010;Nevertheless the links Pascal provided are very interesting. And I found even a few posts&#010;of Jez Humble, the author of that CD book I haven't read yet. :D I will definitely read the&#010;forum discussion and also have a look at the YouTube video.&#010;&#010;Again I want to thank all to all the people who responded to my mail. Now I have some material&#010;to read through and discuss it with my colleagues. I hope you're not getting mad if I come&#010;back for more questions. :)&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Gerrit&#010;&#010;&#010;-----Ursprüngliche Nachricht-----&#010;Von: Pascal Rapicault [mailto:pascal@rapicault.net] &#010;Gesendet: Freitag, 13. Juni 2014 04:32&#010;An: Maven Users List&#010;Betreff: Re: Complex Maven projects - Tutorials? Books?&#010;&#010;If you are really aiming at doing continuous delivery (any potential build can be pushed to&#010;prod), then SNAPSHOT is not a great way to deal with dependencies since you will not be able&#010;to exactly know what you ship. To avoid this, one practice is to use the build number in the&#010;artifact version (1.0.0-b1 or 1.0.1).&#010;This has of course had the drawback that now you have to update the pom.xml of components&#010;using a specific artifact (move from build 1 to 2) but this also gives you greater control&#010;on the rate at which you consume libraries.&#010;You may be interested in these articles:&#010;-&#010;http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Continuous-Delivery-and-Maven-td3245370.html&#010;-&#010;http://stackoverflow.com/questions/18456111/what-is-the-maven-way-for-project-versions-when-doing-continuous-delivery&#010;&#010;That said, if you add Artifactory to the mix, you can leverage its capabilities of obtaining&#010;specific versions of a SNAPSHOT through matrix parameters&#010;(https://www.jfrog.com/confluence/display/RTF/Using+Properties+in+Deployment+and+Resolution)&#010;quite handy. One example where this comes handy is when you split your build process over&#010;multiple jenkins jobs and you want to make sure that you use the same artifact throughout&#010;the process and this w/o blocking the whole "pipeline" for the whole duration of the process.&#010;&#010;HTH&#010;&#010;Pascal&#010;On 12/06/2014 10:46 AM, Hohl, Gerrit wrote:&#010;&gt; Hello everyone, :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have a question which is not about a specific problem with Maven, &#010;&gt; but more a general question.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I hope it is okay to ask this question here.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We use Maven and Jenkins for about 1.5 years now, I guess. Until now &#010;&gt; the Maven projects have been very simple and - let's say - very monolithic.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But recently we identify more and more internal libraries in our &#010;&gt; products. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by &#010;&gt; copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. But &#010;&gt; most of them only deal with simple projects. They don't cover e.g.&#010;&gt; versioning the build process (especially if your build process &#010;&gt; consists of more than just one step). They also don't cover the &#010;&gt; problems of developing the libraries while your developing the &#010;&gt; products which depend on them. Especially at the beginning your &#010;&gt; libraries will go through a lot of changes. A few name snapshots as a &#010;&gt; solution, but don't explain how you can work using them, how you can &#010;&gt; use them in your pom.xml and how you deal with them if you finally &#010;&gt; switch your product and/or your library from the snapshot state to the &#010;&gt; release state. A few also say that you shouldn't use snapshots at all &#010;&gt; because it will result in many problems (e.g. having -SNAPSHOT entries &#010;&gt; in your pom.xml). Nightly builds or build triggered by the SCM are also an issue here.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these &#010;&gt; issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Gerrit&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I though I should share two scripts I hacked together when working with&#010;multiple aggregation roots from different GIT repositories...&#010;&#010;The first one I call `mvn-release-all.rb`&#010;&#010;#!/usr/bin/env ruby&#010;&#010;require 'nokogiri'&#010;&#010;want_color = `git config color.ui`&#010;$color = case want_color.chomp&#010;           when "true";&#010;             true&#010;           when "auto";&#010;             $stdout.tty?&#010;         end&#010;&#010;def red s;&#010;  $color ? "\033[31m#{s}\033[0m" : s&#010;end&#010;&#010;def green s;&#010;  $color ? "\033[32m#{s}\033[0m" : s&#010;end&#010;&#010;def yellow s;&#010;  $color ? "\033[33m#{s}\033[0m" : s&#010;end&#010;&#010;def cyan s;&#010;  $color ? "\033[36m#{s}\033[0m" : s&#010;end&#010;&#010;def grey s;&#010;  $color ? "\033[1;30m#{s}\033[0m" : s&#010;end&#010;&#010;def purple s;&#010;  $color ? "\033[35m#{s}\033[0m" : s&#010;end&#010;&#010;def read_pom pom_file&#010;  Nokogiri::XML(File.open(pom_file)) { |config| config.nonet&#010;}.remove_namespaces!&#010;end&#010;&#010;def group_id pom_doc&#010;  (pom_doc.xpath('/project/groupId').first or&#010;pom_doc.xpath('/project/parent/groupId').first).text&#010;end&#010;&#010;def artifact_id pom_doc&#010;  (pom_doc.xpath('/project/artifactId').first or&#010;pom_doc.xpath('/project/parent/artifactId').first).text&#010;end&#010;&#010;def version pom_doc&#010;  (pom_doc.xpath('/project/version').first or&#010;pom_doc.xpath('/project/parent/version').first).text&#010;end&#010;&#010;def upstream_version pom_doc, coord&#010;  g, a = coord.match(/(^.*):(.*)$/i).captures&#010;  result = []&#010;  pom_doc.xpath('/project/parent').each do |n|&#010;    pg = n.xpath('groupId').first.text&#010;    pa = n.xpath('artifactId').first.text&#010;    pv = n.xpath('version').first.text if n.xpath('version').first&#010;    if g == pg and a == pa and pv&#010;      result &lt;&lt; pv&#010;    end&#010;    break&#010;  end&#010;&#010;pom_doc.xpath('/project/dependencyManagement/dependencies/dependency').each&#010;do |n|&#010;    pg = n.xpath('groupId').first.text&#010;    pa = n.xpath('artifactId').first.text&#010;    pv = n.xpath('version').first.text if n.xpath('version').first&#010;    if g == pg and a == pa and pv&#010;      result &lt;&lt; pv&#010;    end&#010;  end&#010;  pom_doc.xpath('/project/dependencies/dependency').each do |n|&#010;    pg = n.xpath('groupId').first.text&#010;    pa = n.xpath('artifactId').first.text&#010;    pv = n.xpath('version').first.text if n.xpath('version').first&#010;    if g == pg and a == pa and pv&#010;      result &lt;&lt; pv&#010;    end&#010;  end&#010;  result.uniq&#010;end&#010;&#010;def coords pom_doc&#010;  "#{group_id pom_doc}:#{artifact_id pom_doc}"&#010;end&#010;&#010;def upstream_coords pom_doc&#010;  result = []&#010;  pom_doc.xpath('/project/parent').each do |n|&#010;    groupId = n.xpath('groupId').first.text&#010;    artifactId = n.xpath('artifactId').first.text&#010;    result &lt;&lt; "#{groupId}:#{artifactId}"&#010;    break&#010;  end&#010;  pom_doc.xpath('/project/dependencies/dependency').each do |n|&#010;    groupId = n.xpath('groupId').first.text&#010;    artifactId = n.xpath('artifactId').first.text&#010;    result &lt;&lt; "#{groupId}:#{artifactId}"&#010;  end&#010;  result&#010;end&#010;&#010;def release_root? pom_doc&#010;  pom_doc.xpath('/project/scm').first and pom_doc.xpath('/project/version')&#010;end&#010;&#010;def collapse_dependencies dependencies&#010;  result = Hash.new&#010;&#010;  dependencies.each do |coord, deps|&#010;    collapsed_deps = []&#010;    deps.each { |d| collapsed_deps &lt;&lt; d;&#010;    if dependencies[d];&#010;      collapsed_deps = collapsed_deps + dependencies[d]&#010;    end }&#010;    result[coord] = collapsed_deps.uniq&#010;  end&#010;  result&#010;end&#010;&#010;def uncommitted_changes? paths&#010;  result = false;&#010;  paths.each do |path|&#010;    if File.exists?("#{path}/.git")&#010;      status = `git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path} status&#010;--porcelain | sed -ne '/pom.xml.releaseBackup/d;/release.properties/d;p'`&#010;      if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;        puts "#{red "Could not determine status of files in #{path}"}"&#010;        exit 7&#010;      end&#010;      if not status.empty?&#010;        puts "#{yellow "There are uncommitted changes:"}" unless result&#010;        status.split(/\n/).each { |l| s, p = l.match(/(..) (.*)/).captures;&#010;puts "#{s} #{path}/#{p}" }&#010;        result = true&#010;      end&#010;    end&#010;  end&#010;  result&#010;end&#010;&#010;def commit_all paths, message&#010;  paths.each do |path|&#010;    if File.exists?("#{path}/.git")&#010;      status = `git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path} status&#010;--porcelain`&#010;      if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;        puts "Could not determine status of files in #{path}"&#010;        exit 7&#010;      end&#010;      if not status.empty?&#010;        system "git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path} commit -a -m&#010;\"#{message}\""&#010;        if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;          puts "Could not commit changes in #{path}"&#010;          exit 7&#010;        end&#010;        status = `git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path} status&#010;--porcelain`&#010;        if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;          puts "Could not determine status of files in #{path}"&#010;          exit 7&#010;        end&#010;        if not status.empty?&#010;          puts "Did not commit files in #{path}"&#010;          exit 7&#010;        end&#010;        status = `git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path} log -n 1&#010;--pretty='%s' @{u}..`&#010;        if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;          puts "Could not determine status of files in #{path}"&#010;          exit 7&#010;        end&#010;        if not status.empty?&#010;          status = `git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path} push`&#010;          if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;            puts "Could not publish changes in #{path}"&#010;            exit 7&#010;          end&#010;        end&#010;      end&#010;    end&#010;  end&#010;end&#010;&#010;yolo = ""&#010;loop {&#010;  case ARGV[0]&#010;    when '--yolo' then&#010;      ARGV.shift; yolo = "-B"&#010;    else&#010;      break;&#010;  end&#010;}&#010;&#010;&#010;poms = Hash.new&#010;&#010;coord2path = Hash.new&#010;&#010;dependencies = Hash.new&#010;&#010;roots = []&#010;git_roots = []&#010;&#010;modules = ["."]&#010;&#010;modules.each do |path|&#010;  pom_doc = read_pom "#{path}/pom.xml"&#010;  pom_doc.xpath('/project/modules/module').each do |n|&#010;    modules.include?("#{path}/#{n.text}") if modules &lt;&lt; "#{path}/#{n.text}"&#010;  end&#010;  poms[path] = pom_doc&#010;  coord = coords pom_doc&#010;  coord2path[coord] = path&#010;  dependencies[coord] = upstream_coords pom_doc&#010;  # only poms that have scm section AND specify their version rather than&#010;inherit are releasable&#010;  roots &lt;&lt; coord if release_root?(pom_doc)&#010;  git_roots &lt;&lt; coord if File.exists?("#{path}/.git")&#010;end&#010;&#010;dependencies = collapse_dependencies dependencies&#010;&#010;# sort the roots into release tree order&#010;roots.sort! do |a, b|&#010;  case&#010;    when (dependencies[a].include?(b)) &amp;&amp; !(dependencies[b].include?(a))&#010;      1&#010;    when (dependencies[b].include?(a)) &amp;&amp; !(dependencies[a].include?(b))&#010;      -1&#010;    else&#010;      case dependencies[a].size &lt;=&gt; dependencies[b].size&#010;        when -1&#010;          -1&#010;        when 1&#010;          1&#010;        when 0&#010;          a &lt;=&gt; b&#010;      end&#010;  end&#010;end&#010;&#010;exit 1 if uncommitted_changes?(git_roots.map { |e| coord2path[e] })&#010;&#010;last_need_release = nil&#010;need_release = []&#010;begin&#010;  if not need_release.empty?&#010;&#010;    exit 1 if uncommitted_changes?(git_roots.map { |e| coord2path[e] })&#010;&#010;    coord = need_release.first&#010;    g, a = coord.match(/(^.*):(.*)$/i).captures&#010;    path = coord2path[coord]&#010;&#010;    puts "#{green "Detected changes since last release in "} #{yellow&#010;g}:#{yellow a}"&#010;&#010;    system "cd #{path} &amp;&amp; mvn release:prepare release:perform&#010;-DautoVersionSubmodules=true #{yolo}"&#010;    if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;      break&#010;    end&#010;    if File.exists?("#{path}/target/checkout/pom.xml")&#010;      new_version = version(read_pom("#{path}/target/checkout/pom.xml"))&#010;      puts "#{green "Linking downstream projects to version"} #{yellow&#010;new_version}..."&#010;      dependencies.each do |d, dummy|&#010;        pp = coord2path[d]&#010;        if pp &amp;&amp; dependencies[d].include?(coord)&#010;          old_versions = upstream_version(poms[pp], coord) +&#010;upstream_version(read_pom("#{pp}/pom.xml"), coord)&#010;          old_versions.uniq.each do |old_version|&#010;            unless old_version == new_version&#010;              puts "  #{yellow d}"&#010;              cmd = "mvn org.codehaus.mojo:versions-maven-plugin:2.1:set " +&#010;                  "org.codehaus.mojo:versions-maven-plugin:2.1:commit " +&#010;                  "-DgroupId=#{g} " +&#010;                  "-DartifactId=#{a} " +&#010;                  "-DnewVersion=#{new_version} " +&#010;                  "-DoldVersion=#{old_version} " +&#010;                  "-DprocessProject=false " +&#010;                  "-DupdateMatchingVersions=false"&#010;              out = `#{cmd}`&#010;              if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;                puts "Could not update downstream projects:\n#{out}"&#010;                exit 7&#010;              end&#010;              commit_all(git_roots.map { |e| coord2path[e] }, "Updating&#010;#{g}:#{a} from #{old_version} to #{new_version}")&#010;            end&#010;          end&#010;        end&#010;      end&#010;    end&#010;    puts ""&#010;  end&#010;  last_need_release = need_release&#010;  need_release = []&#010;  roots.each do |coord|&#010;    path = coord2path[coord]&#010;  "-DprocessProject=false " +&#010;  "-DupdateMatchingVersions=false"&#010;out = `#{cmd}`&#010;if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;puts "Could not update downstream projects:\n#{out}"&#010;exit 7&#010;end&#010;end&#010;end&#010;    end&#010;end&#010;puts ""&#010;end&#010;last_need_link = need_link&#010;need_link = []&#010;roots.each do |coord|&#010;path = coord2path[coord]&#010;status = `git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path} status --porcelain`&#010;if $?.exitstatus &gt; 0&#010;puts "Could not determine status of files in #{path}"&#010;exit 7&#010;end&#010;unless status.empty? and `git --git-dir #{path}/.git --work-tree #{path}&#010;log -n 1 --pretty='%s'`.match(/^\[maven-release-plugin\] prepare for next&#010;development iteration/) and $?.exitstatus == 0&#010;unless have_link.include?(coord)&#010;need_link &lt;&lt; coord&#010;end&#010;end&#010;end&#010;end while not need_link.empty? and last_need_link != need_link&#010;&#010;&#010;So how do you use these two scripts?&#010;&#010;Well what I tend to do is have a local aggregator project when I am working&#010;on different components. I check out all the components and the local&#010;aggregator project (typically not checked in to SCM) has &lt;module&gt; entries&#010;for each of the different libraries.&#010;&#010;Now normally I'm working away using release versions of the libraries...&#010;but oh look the foobar library has a bug in it. I go and fix the foobar&#010;module... then I run&#010;&#010;$ mvn-link-changed.rb&#010;&#010;And presto, everything gets updated to use the -SNAPSHOT dependencies from&#010;the local aggregator root...&#010;&#010;Now the script is smart enough to only link in modules that have changed&#010;since the last use of the maven release plugin, so most things will stay on&#010;the release version until you update the code.&#010;&#010;When it comes time to push releases&#010;&#010;$ mvn-release-all.rb --yolo&#010;&#010;(You can omit the --yolo option if you want to be prompted by the release&#010;plugin for each SCM root)&#010;&#010;And that will release, in dependency order, all the modules that have&#010;changes since the last release.&#010;&#010;I should probably write this up as a blog post... but my scripts are not&#010;yet as robust as I'd like... they work for me... largely because I have&#010;everything in git&#010;&#010;&#010;On 13 June 2014 09:41, Hohl, Gerrit &lt;g.hohl@aurenz.de&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hello everyone, :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; wow, I got a lot of useful responses. Thanks a lot, Michael, Ron, Barrie&#010;&gt; and Pascal.&#010;&gt; And sorry for the double mail. Seems the mailing list got it twice.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We already have a Nexus running here (v2.6.2-01 - I know: There is&#010;&gt; v2.8.1-01 available) and use it as a mirror / proxy as well as for&#010;&gt; uploading some JAR and POM files which are not available in the public&#010;&gt; repositories.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Instead of the Maven Versions Plugin we came across the Maven Release&#010;&gt; Plugin. This way you can check in all the time, but only once the build&#010;&gt; process creates a stable release by modifying the pom.xml files, building,&#010;&gt; checking in this version of the pom.xml into the SCM, tagging or branching&#010;&gt; this version in the SCM, modifying the pom.xml again (back to snaphots) and&#010;&gt; checking it in again.&#010;&gt; But we asked ourselves if this is really the best solution as it seemed a&#010;&gt; little bit complex and if there isn't a more simple solution for doing that.&#010;&gt; I have to admit that a colleague was working on that issue and not me. I&#010;&gt; will discuss it with him again.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Another colleague and I said the same like Ron wrote. That internal&#010;&gt; libraries should be handled like external ones.&#010;&gt; Our problem at the moment is that the libraries as well as the application&#010;&gt; change every day. We don't have separated teams for applications and&#010;&gt; libraries - we are too small for that. On the other side other developers&#010;&gt; of the team have to rely on changes which are made. So we have to publish&#010;&gt; them to the SCM. Here we face the problem that we also have to deploy them&#010;&gt; to Nexus as the other party maybe only works on one project, but doesn't&#010;&gt; have the library checked out from the SCM at the same time. So if project A&#010;&gt; is checked in you also have to deploy library B. Otherwise the other&#010;&gt; developer which checks out project A won't be able to start it, maybe even&#010;&gt; to compile it, because project A in the SCM depends on a newer library B&#010;&gt; version than the developer has in his local repository.&#010;&gt; My argument in the discussion back then was that this should be solved by&#010;&gt; snapshots. Especially if you have a build server which is triggered by&#010;&gt; changes in the SCM you would be able to have the newest version of the&#010;&gt; library always available in your Nexus repository.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We read many articles on the Internet so far. And we read the following&#010;&gt; books:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Maven 2 - Eine Einführung, aktuell zur Version 2.0.9 (Maven 2 - An&#010;&gt; introduction)&#010;&gt; Author: Kai Uwe Bachmann&#010;&gt; Publisher: Addision-Wesley&#010;&gt; ISBN: 978-3-8273-2835-9&#010;&gt; It is a really only an introduction and many things are not mentioned or&#010;&gt; discusses in that book. Kai talks only about very simply examples. He&#010;&gt; doesn't write about more complex problems you will face for sure if you&#010;&gt; work a little bit longer and maybe on bigger projects using Maven.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Jenkins - kurz &amp; gut&#010;&gt; Author: Mario Behrendt&#010;&gt; Publisher: O'Reilly&#010;&gt; ISBN: 978-3-86899-127-7&#010;&gt; This books is not directly related to Maven, but also mentions it. It is a&#010;&gt; short overview of CI using Jenkins. I guess you won't get Jenkins running&#010;&gt; if you only read this book. But maybe it is a good help for making a&#010;&gt; decision if you want to use Jenkins or not.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Jenkins - The Definitive Guide&#010;&gt; Author: John Ferguson Smart&#010;&gt; Publisher: O'Reilly&#010;&gt; ISBN: 978-1-449-30535-2&#010;&gt; Also not directly related to Maven, but explain how to use Jenkins and&#010;&gt; Maven together.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I also bought recently:&#010;&gt; Continuous Delivery: Reliable Software Releases Through Build, Test, and&#010;&gt; Deployment Automation&#010;&gt; Authors: Jez Humble, David Farley&#010;&gt; Publisher: Addision-Wesley&#010;&gt; ISBN: 978-0321601919&#010;&gt; I haven't read it yet. But I hope to get a deeper understanding of the&#010;&gt; whole process. But I'm not sure if it will help me solving our problems.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I had a look on the books on the Maven site. Most look like they are&#010;&gt; already old and dealing with Maven 2 (like the book we have - unfortunately&#010;&gt; - also does). And the newest one got some poor reviews (okay, they are&#010;&gt; subjective, so maybe the book isn't that bad). Maybe one of you can give a&#010;&gt; recommendation for a book which is not dedicated to beginners, but instead&#010;&gt; handles some issues of developers who are already on the next level (but&#010;&gt; not on the highest level yet).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Of course we are also reading the online documentation. But I have to&#010;&gt; admit that it sometimes lacks the one or another information which you find&#010;&gt; in some blogs or articles after some search. And some of the 3rd party&#010;&gt; plugins are explained really poorly (okay, that is not a problem of the&#010;&gt; Maven project). That doesn't make it easier as Maven offers some many&#010;&gt; possibilities and therefore *can* get complex.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We also found a presentation on the Internet which described a solution&#010;&gt; like Pascal mentioned in his mail. But doesn't that mean that you will have&#010;&gt; hundreds and hundreds of releases in your repository? And doesn't it mean&#010;&gt; you have to update the pom.xml files of your projects which are developed&#010;&gt; simultaneously all the time? Somehow I prefer the idea - like Ron - of&#010;&gt; handling internal libraries not different from external libraries. But I&#010;&gt; also see the points of people who argument for the CD way-of-life.&#010;&gt; Nevertheless the links Pascal provided are very interesting. And I found&#010;&gt; even a few posts of Jez Humble, the author of that CD book I haven't read&#010;&gt; yet. :D I will definitely read the forum discussion and also have a look at&#010;&gt; the YouTube video.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Again I want to thank all to all the people who responded to my mail. Now&#010;&gt; I have some material to read through and discuss it with my colleagues. I&#010;&gt; hope you're not getting mad if I come back for more questions. :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt; Gerrit&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -----Ursprüngliche Nachricht-----&#010;&gt; Von: Pascal Rapicault [mailto:pascal@rapicault.net]&#010;&gt; Gesendet: Freitag, 13. Juni 2014 04:32&#010;&gt; An: Maven Users List&#010;&gt; Betreff: Re: Complex Maven projects - Tutorials? Books?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If you are really aiming at doing continuous delivery (any potential build&#010;&gt; can be pushed to prod), then SNAPSHOT is not a great way to deal with&#010;&gt; dependencies since you will not be able to exactly know what you ship. To&#010;&gt; avoid this, one practice is to use the build number in the artifact version&#010;&gt; (1.0.0-b1 or 1.0.1).&#010;&gt; This has of course had the drawback that now you have to update the&#010;&gt; pom.xml of components using a specific artifact (move from build 1 to 2)&#010;&gt; but this also gives you greater control on the rate at which you consume&#010;&gt; libraries.&#010;&gt; You may be interested in these articles:&#010;&gt; -&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Continuous-Delivery-and-Maven-td3245370.html&#010;&gt; -&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; http://stackoverflow.com/questions/18456111/what-is-the-maven-way-for-project-versions-when-doing-continuous-delivery&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That said, if you add Artifactory to the mix, you can leverage its&#010;&gt; capabilities of obtaining specific versions of a SNAPSHOT through matrix&#010;&gt; parameters&#010;&gt; (&#010;&gt; https://www.jfrog.com/confluence/display/RTF/Using+Properties+in+Deployment+and+Resolution&#010;&gt; )&#010;&gt; quite handy. One example where this comes handy is when you split your&#010;&gt; build process over multiple jenkins jobs and you want to make sure that you&#010;&gt; use the same artifact throughout the process and this w/o blocking the&#010;&gt; whole "pipeline" for the whole duration of the process.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; HTH&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Pascal&#010;&gt; On 12/06/2014 10:46 AM, Hohl, Gerrit wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; Hello everyone, :)&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I have a question which is not about a specific problem with Maven,&#010;&gt; &gt; but more a general question.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I hope it is okay to ask this question here.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; We use Maven and Jenkins for about 1.5 years now, I guess. Until now&#010;&gt; &gt; the Maven projects have been very simple and - let's say - very&#010;&gt; monolithic.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; But recently we identify more and more internal libraries in our&#010;&gt; &gt; products. Of course we don't want to share this libraries by&#010;&gt; &gt; copy-n-paste between the products - especially as we have Maven.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; So we started to read books, tutorials on the Internet and so on. But&#010;&gt; &gt; most of them only deal with simple projects. They don't cover e.g.&#010;&gt; &gt; versioning the build process (especially if your build process&#010;&gt; &gt; consists of more than just one step). They also don't cover the&#010;&gt; &gt; problems of developing the libraries while your developing the&#010;&gt; &gt; products which depend on them. Especially at the beginning your&#010;&gt; &gt; libraries will go through a lot of changes. A few name snapshots as a&#010;&gt; &gt; solution, but don't explain how you can work using them, how you can&#010;&gt; &gt; use them in your pom.xml and how you deal with them if you finally&#010;&gt; &gt; switch your product and/or your library from the snapshot state to the&#010;&gt; &gt; release state. A few also say that you shouldn't use snapshots at all&#010;&gt; &gt; because it will result in many problems (e.g. having -SNAPSHOT entries&#010;&gt; &gt; in your pom.xml). Nightly builds or build triggered by the SCM are also&#010;&gt; an issue here.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Does someone know a good book or tutorial which handles all of these&#010;&gt; &gt; issues around Maven and CI/CD in more depth?&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Regards,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Gerrit&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Hi Andy,&#010;&#010;First of all: welcome in the world of Apache Maven!&#010;I won't go into detail too much right now, I'd suggest to do some  &#010;getting-started tutorials[2] to understand the basics.&#010;&#010;Let's start with:&#010;With Maven you can call 2 things: a phase of a lifecycle[1] or a goal from  &#010;a specific plugin.&#010;if you're running 'mvn deploy:deploy-file' you're only executing 1 goal.&#010;And 'mvn deploy' means you're executing all phases up to deploy,  &#010;representing a chain of goals.&#010;&#010;Since you're using an execution-block I assume you just want to call 'mvn  &#010;deploy'.&#010;&#010;thanks,&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;[1]  &#010;http://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-the-lifecycle.html&#010;[2] http://maven.apache.org/guides/index.html&#010;&#010;Op Tue, 17 Jun 2014 00:51:21 +0200 schreef Andrew Davidson  &#010;&lt;adavidson2@apple.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I recently joined an existing project that uses the maven ant plug into  &#010;&gt; to build artifacts that we need to distribute. org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-deploy-plugin:2.8:deploy-file  &#010;&gt; (default-cli) on project mary-aide-dist: The parameters 'file' for goal  &#010;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-deploy-plugin:2.8:deploy-file are missing  &#010;&gt; or invalid -&gt; [Help 1]&#010;&gt; [ERROR]&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I have tried using -X and -e how ever I can still can not figure out  &#010;&gt; what the problem is.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; any idea what I am doing wrong? &#009;&#009;&#009;&#009;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; thanks&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Andy&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;distributionManagement&gt; … &lt;/&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;properties&gt;&#010;&gt; &#009;&lt;mary-aide-proxy.tar&gt;mary-aide-proxy-${project.version}&lt;/mary-aide-proxy.tar&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Subject  :-
Running plugin with &quot;own&quot; classloader for slf4j in maven 3.2  
Date  :-
Tue, 17 Jun 2014 19:34:23 GMT  
contents:- 
Until Maven 3.0.x it was possible to run plugins that use slf4j with a&#010;configuration of slf4j chosen by the project files (e.g. slf4j log4j binding&#010;or a simplelogging config in the project), since Maven wasn't using slf4j&#010;itself. Now in 3.2, the slf4j classes are loaded by Maven and so use the&#010;ones that are stored in the lib and config dirs of Maven.&#010;&#010;It is possible to remove the slf4j related files from maven and use other&#010;ones instead, but I would prefer it if I could select the binding inside the&#010;project. I assume that this requires some kind of classpath change to force&#010;the plugin to use a new instance of slf4j and use the files select in the&#010;project, but I have no idea how to do that (or if it is possible at all).&#010;&#010;(the plugin I am currently using is vertx-maven-plugin, which basically runs&#010;the whole project inside Maven)&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Running-plugin-with-own-classloader-for-slf4j-in-maven-3-2-tp5796426.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

I understand that you have a few (120) repos but once you have made the &#010;list, it is easy to maintain.&#010;Same as the list of active projects. 1000 is a lot of names to list but &#010;you probably can find one already existing or make one through a &#010;partially automated process.&#010;&#010;Otherwise it is a clerical task that you can give to a junior tech.&#010;DEPARTMENT_POM -&gt;TEAM_POM -&gt; PROJECT_POM -&gt; MODULE_POM&#010;is more interesting but probably not that hard to manage.&#010;&#010;DEPARTMENT_POM -&gt;TEAM_POM is a small list.&#010;You want to eliminate duplicate sub-trees.&#010;&#010;Just a suggestion for a non-maven solution. Ron,&#010;&#010;we have developed some tools which try to guess POM resolutions using&#010;Python and getting the same resolution resp. interpolations as Maven&#010;is sometimes hard to do:&#010;&#010;* Inheriting POMs do not need to override version and groupId so you&#010;have to interpolate these from the ancestors.&#010;* Same for properties which are inherited as well while other elements&#010;as scm are adding module/artifactIds.&#010;&#010;Regards&#010;Mirko&#010;Regards Mirko&#010;--&#010;http://illegalstateexception.blogspot.com/&#010;https://github.com/mfriedenhagen/ (http://osrc.dfm.io/mfriedenhagen)&#010;https://bitbucket.org/mfriedenhagen/&#010;&#010;&#010;On Fri, Jun 20, 2014 at 6:49 PM, Ron Wheeler&#010;&lt;rwheeler@artifact-software.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; I understand that you have a few (120) repos but once you have made the&#010;&gt; list, it is easy to maintain.&#010;&gt; Same as the list of active projects. 1000 is a lot of names to list but you&#010;&gt; probably can find one already existing or make one through a partially&#010;&gt; automated process.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Otherwise it is a clerical task that you can give to a junior tech.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; DEPARTMENT_POM -&gt;TEAM_POM -&gt; PROJECT_POM -&gt; MODULE_POM&#010;&gt; is more interesting but probably not that hard to manage.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; DEPARTMENT_POM -&gt;TEAM_POM is a small list.&#010;&gt; You want to eliminate duplicate sub-trees.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Just a suggestion for a non-maven solution. That is one of the advantages of&#010;&gt; using XML in the POM,&#010;&gt; You are not restricted to using the application for which the files are&#010;&gt; designed.&#010;&gt; There are lots of XML tools - both low level and high level that can be&#010;&gt; Name  :- 
Ben Podgursky &lt;bpodgur...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: plugin execution &amp; phase/goal selection question  
Date  :-
Tue, 24 Jun 2014 04:17:48 GMT  
contents:- 
Your goal would just be the goal from the antrun plugin that you want to&#010;execute (in this case "run").  If you look at the list of lifecycle phases (&#010;http://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-the-lifecycle.html),&#010;you could bind your execution to whichever phase makes most sense (say,&#010;process-resources).  So working with the example from the antrun usage (&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-antrun-plugin/usage.html), you'd get&#010;something like:&#010;&#010;      &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;        &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-antrun-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;        &lt;version&gt;1.7&lt;/version&gt;&#010;        &lt;executions&gt;&#010;          &lt;execution&gt;&#010;            &lt;phase&gt; process-sources &lt;/phase&gt;&#010;            &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;              &lt;target&gt;&#010;                &lt;!--&#010;                  your ant code&#010;                --&gt;&#010;              &lt;/target&gt;&#010;            &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;            &lt;goals&gt;&#010;              &lt;goal&gt;run&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;            &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;          &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;        &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;      &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;so you're telling maven, run the "run" goal with this ant code during phase&#010;process-sources.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Jun 23, 2014 at 1:09 PM, kathyczv &lt;kathyczv@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have a POM with packaging set to 'war'.&#010;&gt; I want to run 'antrun' plugin just before the code is compiled. What do I&#010;&gt; set the plugin's phase and goal to?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; My understanding is that the phase is one of the war's phases, for example:&#010;&gt; 'process-resources'&#010;&gt; Or a default one, for example: 'initialize'&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; How about the goal, is that one of the antrun's goals?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Your help is appreciated!&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

[ANN] Apache Maven JAR Plugin 2.5 Released  
Date  :-
Tue, 24 Jun 2014 10:20:30 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the &#010;Apache Maven JAR Plugin, version 2.5.&#010;&#010;This plugin provides the capability to build jars.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-jar-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-jar-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.5&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven JAR Plugin - Version 2.5&#010;&#010;Bugs:&#010;&#010;    [MJAR-157] - forceUpdate documentation is insufficient&#010;    [MJAR-162] - skipIfEmpty not work for test-jar goal and empty directories&#010;    [MJAR-167] - skipIfEmpty outputs incorrect logging nessage&#010;&#010;Improvements:&#010;&#010;    [MJAR-168] - Update to latest plexus-archiver&#010;    [MJAR-170] - please add property 'maven.jar.classifier'&#010;    [MJAR-175] - Documentation problem for test-jar&#010;    [MJAR-176] - Usage page should (only) describe default behavior&#010;&#010;Tasks:&#010;&#010;    [MJAR-158] - use maven-plugin-tools' java 5 annotations&#010;    [MJAR-171] - Remove deprecated mojo jar-sign and jar-sign-verify&#010;    [MJAR-173] - Check correctness of declared deps&#010;&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi&#010;&#010;I am seeking for help from Maven with Perforce SCM to test out test p4maven&#010;scm provider&#010;which is being refactor ( very close to completion) with the following&#010;improvements&#010;&#010;    * Auto discover the existing Perforce client that manages the checked&#010;out Maven source tree.&#010;      User is no longer required to configure the client name via Java&#010;system properties&#010;&#010;    * Generate clients are auto destroyed after each JVM session.( ie auto&#010;cleanup)&#010;&#010;    * Full integration with Release plugin. User now can release Maven&#010;project with Perforce SCM using one command ( mvn -B release:preare&#010;release:perform)&#010;&#010;    * Comply with Maven SCM Technology Compatibility Kit (TCK)&#010;&#010;    * Added Lots of Maven Plugin Integration Tests.&#010;&#010;&#010;The source is at workshop.perforce.com:1666://guest/dantran/p4maven&#010;&#010;the webview is&#010;https://swarm.workshop.perforce.com/files/guest/dantran/p4maven&#010;&#010;&#010;Your feedback are very much appreciated.&#010;&#010;-Dan&#010;&#010;PS: I am in the process working perforce opensource to deploy p4maven&#010;Sonatype snapshot repo.&#010;&#010;
